TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-565 
 
AUTHORIZES THE REMOVAL OF ALL WEEDS IN EXCESS OF 10 INCHES, YARD 
WASTE, LITTER, GARBAGE/REFUSE, RUBBISH, RUBBISH, UPON THE 
PREMISES KNOWN AS 262 HULSE AVENUE, WADING RIVER, NEW YORK, 
SUFFOLK COUNTY TAX MAP#: 0600-033.00-05.00-027.000 PURSUANT TO 
RIVERHEAD TOWN CODE CHAPTER 251 
 
Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
WHEREAS, Chapter 251 of the Code of the Town of Riverhead (Riverhead Town 
Code) entitled, "Rubbish, Refuse, Weeds and Other Rank Vegetation" authorizes the 
Riverhead Town Board to direct removal of rubbish, litter, garbage/refuse upon the land 
by the owner, renter or occupier of the premises; and 
 
WHEREAS, that pursuant to §251 -18 of the Riverhead Town Code, the legislative 
intent of the Town Board is to minimize unsightly conditions and environmental public 
nuisance(s), and to provide minimum requirements to safeguard public safety, health 
and general welfare insofar as they are affected by any undesirable, environmental 
public nuisance(s) or condition(s) of blight on such land(s), premises and public way(s) 
and whereby reasons that such conditions may cause a fire hazard, create a nuisance 
to children with potential danger of injury on rocks, debris, holes, noxious weeds, etc., 
obstruct visibility at street intersections, result in the aggravation of allergies or furnish a 
potential harborage or breeding place for disease -carrying insects, arthropods, animals 
and snakes covered by excess growth or vegetation; and it is further, 
 
WHEREAS, On May 8, 2025 Riverhead Code Officer, Nicole Buckner observed 
weeds in excess of 10 inches, yard waste, rubbish, litter, garbage/refuse at premises 
known as 262 Hulse Avenue, Wading River, New York, known and designated as 
Suffolk County Tax Map as 0600-033.00-05.00-027.000; and 
 
WHEREAS, Riverhead Town Code Enforcement Official (CEO) Nicole Buckner duly 
issued and posted a Notice of Violation pursuant to Chapter 251 of the Riverhead Town 
Code dated May 8, 2025 placing the owner of 262 Hulse Avenue, Wading River, Suffolk 
County, New York, SCTM # 0600 -033.00-05.00-027.000 on notice of the existence 
and/or persistence of such violations; and 
 
WHEREAS, on May 19, 2025, Code Officer, Nicole Buckner re -inspected the 
property and further determined that the accumulation of weeds in excess of 10 inches, 
yard waste, rubbish, litter, garbage/refuse have not been corrected and/or remedied in 
accordance with the timeframe specified in the notice at the premises known as 262 
Hulse Avenue, Wading River, Suffolk County, New York, SCTM # 0600 -033.00-05.00-
027.000; and   
 
9.55
Packet Pg. 212
WHEREAS, the Owner has failed has failed and neglected or refused to eliminate 
the aforementioned violations of Chapter 251-22 (B); 
 
WHEREAS, pursuant to Riverhead Town Code §251-25 the Riverhead Town Board 
is empowered to adopt a resolution authorizing the removal of all rubbish, litter, 
garbage/refuse which creates a nuisance and furthermore authorizes entry onto such 
premises where such violation exists for the purposes of remedying such violation and 
to charge the cost or expense of such remediation against the owner of said premise; 
and 
 
WHEREAS, pursuant to the Riverhead Town Code §251 -25 C the Riverhead Town 
Board is authorized to reimburse general town funds for the cost of any work performed 
or the services rendered by the Town of Riverhead, for said remediation to such 
violations set forth, at its direction by assessment or levy (lien) upon lots or parcels of 
land where such work was performed and/or such violation exists for services rendered; 
and  
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED,  that the Town Board of the Town of 
Riverhead hereby finds that the real property at 262 Hulse Avenue, Wading River, 
Suffolk County, New York, SCTM # 0600 -033.00-05.00-027.000, is in violation of 
Chapter 251 of the Riverhead Town Code, poses a fire hazard and constitutes a 
nuisance as defined in §251 -21 of the Riverhead Town Code in that real property 
contains weeds in excess of 10 inches, yard waste, rubbish, litter, garbage/refuse; and it 
is further 
 
RESOLVED, that pursuant §251-18 entitled, Legislative Intent and pursuant to  the 
statutory notice provisions as specified in §251 -25 (B) of the Riverhead Town Code as 
mentioned hereinabove, The Riverhead Town Board directs the Town Engineering 
Department to facilitate the entry onto the property designated as 262 Hulse Avenue, 
Wading River, Suffolk County, New York, SCTM # 0600 -033.00-05.00-027.000 in any 
manner deemed appropriate, for the purposes of the removal and or remediation of 
such violations or nuisance conditions as mentioned hereinabove; and it is further,  
 
RESOLVED, pursuant to the Riverhead Town Code §251 -25 (C), The Riverhead 
Town Board directs the Town Engineering Department to prepare an itemization of such 
costs necessary for the removal and remediation of the aforesaid nuisance conditions 
and to further provide a copy of such costs to the Town’s Financial Administrator and 
the Town Assessor no later (60) days after the adoption of this resolution, and it is 
further, 
 
RESOLVED, that the office of the Town of Riverhead Financial Administrator after 
receiving the itemization of such costs from the Town Engineering Department, hereby 
has the authority to establish the appropriate budget for the revenue and expenditure as 
reasonably requested by the Town Engineering Department by preparing a separate 
budget resolution within thirty (30) days of receipt thereof, to be presented before a 
meeting of the Town Board for the approval and adoption relating to such costs 
associated with the entry, removal and remediation deemed necessary to mitigate the 
violations or nuisance conditions upon the property as mentioned hereinabove; and it is 
further, 
 
RESOLVED, that pursuant to the Riverhead Town Code §251 -25 (C) the total 
costs and expenses reported to the Assessor of the Town be assessed against the 
9.55
Packet Pg. 213
premises, and the expense so assessed shall constitute a lien and charge on the 
premises on which it is levied until paid or otherwise satisfied or discharged and shall be 
collected in the same manner and at the same time as other Town charges; and it is 
further, 
  
RESOLVED that pursuant to statutory notice requirements the Riverhead Town 
Board directs the Town Clerk to forward copy(s) of this resolution by email and hard 
copy to the Town Engineering Department, The Town Receiver of Taxes, The Office of 
the Financial Administrator as well as the Town Assessor; and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED that pursuant to statutory notice requirements the Riverhead Town 
Board directs the Town Clerk to also forward a copy(s) of this resolution to the last 
known address, if any, of the Owner of the subject premise as mentioned hereinabove 
as the same may appear on the records of the Receiver of Taxes of the Town by 
mailing a copy forthwith; and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of this 
resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified copy of same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
SECONDER: Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

land where such work was performed and/or such violation exists for services rendered; 
and  
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED,  that the Town Board of the Town of 
Riverhead hereby finds that the real property at 219 Hubbard Avenue, Riverhead, 
Suffolk County, New York, SCTM # 0600 -111.00-04.00-022.000, is in violation of 
Chapter 251 of the Riverhead Town Code, poses a fire hazard and constitutes a 
nuisance as defined in §251 -21 of the Riverhead Town Code in that real property 
contains weeds in excess of 10 inches, yard waste, rubbish, litter, garbage/refuse; and it 
is further 
 
RESOLVED, that pursuant §251-18 entitled, Legislative Intent and pursuant to  the 
statutory notice provisions as specified in §251 -25 (B) of the Riverhead Town Code as 
mentioned hereinabove, The Riverhead Town Board directs the Town Engineering 
Department to facilitate the entry onto the property designated as 219 Hubbard Avenue, 
Riverhead, Suffolk County, New York, SCTM # 0600 -111.00-04.00-022.000 in any 
manner deemed appropriate, for the purposes of the removal and or remediation of 
such violations or nuisance conditions as mentioned hereinabove; and it is further,  
 
RESOLVED, pursuant to the Riverhead Town Code §251 -25 (C), The Riverhead 
Town Board directs the Town Engineering Department to prepare an itemization of such 
costs necessary for the removal and remediation of the aforesaid nuisance conditions 
and to further provide a copy of such costs to the Town’s Financial Administrator and 
the Town Assessor no later (60) days after the adoption of this resolution, and it is 
further, 
 
RESOLVED, that the office of the Town of Riverhead Financial Administrator after 
receiving the itemization of such costs from the Town Engineering Department, hereby 
has the authority to establish the appropriate budget for the revenue and expenditure as 
reasonably requested by the Town Engineering Department by preparing a separate 
budget resolution within thirty (30) days of receipt thereof, to be presented before a 
meeting of the Town Board for the approval and adoption relating to such costs 
associated with the entry, removal and remediation deemed necessary to mitigate the 
violations or nuisance conditions upon the property as mentioned hereinabove; and it is 
further, 
 
RESOLVED, that pursuant to the Riverhead Town Code §251 -25 (C) the total 
costs and expenses reported to the Assessor of the Town be assessed against the 
9.56

premises, and the expense so assessed shall constitute a lien and charge on the 
premises on which it is levied until paid or otherwise satisfied or discharged and shall be

further, 
  
RESOLVED that pursuant to statutory notice requirements the Riverhead Town

WHEREAS, the Town wishes to reorganize the structure of the Accounting 
Department and  designate the position of Payroll Supervisor as a managerial position; 
and 
  
WHEREAS, Melissa Peeker is presently employed by the Town of Riverhead as 
a Payroll Supervisor in a civil service position; and  
 
WHEREAS, the president of the Riverhead CSEA has agreed to stipulate that 
Melissa Peeker may be removed from the labor union to serve as a confidential 
employee in a managerial position in the Accounting Department. 
  
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED,  that effective retroactive to June 15, 
2025, this Town Board hereby appoints Payroll Supervisor, Melissa Peeker to a 
managerial position in the Accounting Department and further authorizes the Town 
Supervisor to enter into a contract agreement with Peeker and execute a stipulation with 
the CSEA in a form substantially similar to the agreement and stipulation attached 
hereto: and be it further,

resolution to Personnel Director, CSEA Unit President, Melissa Peeker, the Town 
Attorney’s Office and the Financial Administrator; and

resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.

9.58
Packet Pg. 225
STIPULATION BETWEEN THE TOWN OF RIVERHEAD & LOCAL 1000, AFSCME, 
AFL-CIO, RIVERHEAD UNIT OF THE SUFFOLK LOCAL #852 
 
This Stipulation is made this ______ day of June, 2025, between the Town of Riverhead 
and the Civil Service Employees Association, Inc., Local 1000, AFSCME, AFL-CIO, Riverhead 
Unit of the Suffolk Local #852 (“the CSEA”).  
 
WHEREAS, the Town’s Payroll Supervisor currently operates in the Accounting 
Department under the supervision of the Financial Administrator; and  
 
WHEREAS,  the Payroll Supervisor works independently and is responsible for preparing 
and distributing payroll to Town employees and handling confidential payroll matters; and 
 
WHEREAS, over the years, the duties and responsibilities of the Payroll Supervisor have 
increasingly required work outside of the standard work-day to address pressing or time-sensitive 
issues, manage volume and research and resolve any payroll issues; and 
  
WHEREAS, based upon the above, the Town desires to reorganize the structure of the 
Accounting Department and designate the position of Payroll Supervisor as a managerial position; 
and  
  
WHEREAS, following a series of communications and negotiations, the Town and 
Civil Employees Association, Inc., Local 1000, AFSCME, AFL-CIO, Riverhead Unit of the 
Suffolk Local #852 desire to enter into this stipulation regarding the appointment of Melissa 
Peeker, presently a unit member, designating her position as managerial and permitting the Town 
to enter into an employment contract with Ms. Peeker and   
 
NOW, THEREFORE, it is mutually agreed as follows:  
 
1. Effective upon the complete ratification of this Agreement, together with a Town 
Board Resolution, the Payroll Supervisor, Melissa Peeker shall be appointed to a 
managerial position and enter into an employment agreement setting terms and 
conditions of employment with the Town. 
2. This Agreement constitutes the entire agreement between the Town and the 
CSEA regarding its subject matter. No other promises or agreements, oral or 
otherwise, have been made.  
3. This Agreement, including this paragraph, may only be modified by written 
agreement executed by the parties and ratified via a Town Board resolution.  
4. This Agreement may be executed with original signatures in counterparts, or by 
facsimile or PDF-scanned signatures in counterparts, which will be deemed legally 
binding as fully as an original signature.  
5. This Agreement is subject to ratification by the Town Board via a duly adopted 
resolution. 
                                                                                                      
____________________________     __________________________  
Timothy C. Hubbard, Supervisor                      Terri DeFilippis, CSEA President 
 
 
                                                                 
Melissa Peeker      Gretchen Penn, LRS 
9.58.a
Packet Pg. 226
Attachment: Stipulation TOR  CSEA re_Peeker  (2025-568 : Sets Terms & Conditions of Employment for a Payroll Supervisor)
 
 
Page 1 of 9 
 
 
Agreement made and entered into t his ______ d ay of June, 2025  THE TOWN OF 
RIVERHEAD, County of Suffolk, State of New York, hereinafter referred to as the "Town", and 
Melissa Peeker, Payroll Supervisor for the Town of Riverhead, New York, hereinafter referred to as 
“Peeker”  
 
 
 W I T N E S S E T H: 
 
WHEREAS, the Town desires to provide Peeker in her capacity as Town Payroll Supervisor 
with written terms and conditions of employment in order to enhance administrative stability and 
continuity within the Town, which the Town believes generally improves the quality of its overall 
mission; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Town and Peeker believe that written terms and conditions of employment 
are necessary to describe specifically their relationship and to serve as the basis of effective 
communication between them as they fulfill their governance and administrative functions in the 
operation of the Town; and 
 
WHEREAS, this Agreement supersedes all prior agreements between the parties; and 
 
WHEREAS, this Agreement cannot be, in whole or in part, amended orally by the parties. 
 
NOW THEREFORE, in exchange of the mutual covenants and considerations, it is agreed 
that the terms and conditions of employment of  Peeker while employed in her position as Town 
Payroll Supervisor shall be as follows: 
 
 
 
 ARTICLE I 
 
 DURATION 
 
1. This Agreement shall be effective as of  June 15, 2025 pursuant to Town Board Resolution 
#2025-______ adopted on June 17, 2025 and shall continue in full force and effect during the period 
of time Peeker serves as the Town Payroll Supervisor. The terms and conditions set forth in Articles 
III, IV, and V with respect to personal time, vacation and sick time shall be prorated for the 2025 
calendar year. 
 
 
 
 
9.58.b
Packet Pg. 227
Attachment: Melissa Peeker Agreement  (2025-568 : Sets Terms & Conditions of Employment for a Payroll Supervisor)
 
 
Page 2 of 9 
 ARTICLE II 
 
 RECOGNITION 
 
1.  The Town recognizes the Peeker’s right to bargain for the terms and conditions of her 
employment with the Town.  Both parties acknowledge that this Agreement is personal to Peeker 
and shall not inure to her successor.  Such recognition is for the period of t his Agreement or 
extensions hereof.  
 
2. Peeker affirms that she does not assert the right to strike against the Town, or to assist or 
participate in any such strike, picket, job action or any work slowdown. 
 
3.  The Town recognizes Peeker’s right to designate a representative to appear on her behalf 
to discuss salaries, working conditions, grievances and disputes relative to the terms and conditions 
of this Agreement and to confer with Peeker during working hours.  The representative's activities 
shall not disrupt the orderly and smooth operation of Town government. 
 
  
 ARTICLE III 
 
 HOURS OF WORK 
 
1.  Peeker’s minimum basic work week shall be  35 hours per week.  There shall be no 
maximum number of hours of work per week.  Peeker shall not receive additional compensation for 
holiday pay.  Peeker is not entitled to earn, accrue, or be paid for overtime or compensatory time.  
 
2.  Peeker shall be en titled to the same paid holidays as those which are set forth in the 
schedule of holidays incorporated in the CSEA collective bargaining agreement with the Town.  
 
3. (a) Five (5) days personal leave will be granted.  
 
    (b)  Personal leave may not be accumulated and must be used within the calendar year 
earned, except that unused personal days at the end of each year shall be converted to sick time 
and may be used as sick time, subject to all the rules and pertaining to sick time. 
 
    (c)  Personal leave must be approved by her Department Head or Town Supervisor. Peeker 
must request such leave at least forty -eight (48) hours in advance unless the personal leave is 
deemed to be an emergency of which she had no prior knowledge, in which case Peeker must notify 
her Department Head of such absence. Failure to notify her supervisor of her absence will result in 
loss of pay for the day's absence. 
 
4.  Funeral Leave.  Peeker shall be entitled to four (4) consecutive working days leave of 
absence computed either from the day of death or the day following death, at Peeker’s option, for the 
death of Peeker’s spouse, child (including adopted children), father, mother, brother, sister, parents, 
9.58.b
Packet Pg. 228
Attachment: Melissa Peeker Agreement  (2025-568 : Sets Terms & Conditions of Employment for a Payroll Supervisor)
 
 
Page 3 of 9 
parents-in-law, grandparents, grandparents-in-law, grandchildren, daughter-in-law, brother-in-law, 
sister-in-law, son-in-law, or stepchild. In the event the Town modifies the terms of the collective 
bargaining agreement with the CSEA, this subparagraph 4 shall be interpreted and deemed modified 
such that it is consistent with such amendment to the CBA.  
 
5.  Jury Service. Peeker will be paid her regular salary while performing jury service upon 
documentary proof being filed with the Supervisor. Peeker shall endorse the jury salary checks to the 
Town.  Travel allowance or mileage compensation checks for jury service are to be retained by  
Peeker. 
 
6.  Court Appearance. Peeker’s absence by reason of appearance as a defendant or witness on 
behalf of the Town in any court action involving the Town will be approved by the Town Supervisor 
for the number of days necessary. Peeker shall not lose any salary there from. 
 
7.  Parentage Leave.  Peeker shall receive a parentage leave as defined in the 20 23-2025 
CSEA contract, Article III, Section 5. 
 
 ARTICLE IV 
 
 VACATIONS 
 
1.  Peeker shall be entitled to 25 working days' vacation (January 1 to December 31).  This 
shall be prorated in 2025.   
 
2.  Peeker, upon request, shall be paid her vacation pay prior to the vacation, providing she 
shall have given three (3) weeks' written notice to the Supervisor. 
 
3.  Upon retirement or termination of service, except for cause, Peeker shall be compensated, 
in cash, for any accumulated vacation not to exceed 60 days. 
 
4.  Peeker may carry over any unused vacation days from one (1) year into the following 
year, but in no event shall Peeker carry over more than sixty (60) vacation days from one year to the 
next. 
 
            5. Peeker, at her option, shall be entitled to make an election to work the current year's 
allotted vacation time. Peeker must provide written notification to the Supervisor of the exercising 
of this option not fewer than thirty (30) days prior to the date of which payment is requested. The 
Supervisor is to acknowledge receipt of this notification to the payroll personnel prior to payment. 
Payment is to be processed during the next overtime run. Payment will be the same method as 
outlined in the 2012-2015 Superior Officers' Contract, Article IX, Section B, except that the 
buyback shall be in blocks of three days per month. “In addition, Peeker must advise the Town in 
writing, by no later than September 1 prior to the year in which the election is being made, on a 
form to be prepared by the Town, of the total minimum and the maximum dollar amounts of 
eligible vacation time and/or sick leave, as appropriate, that the employee will buyout and for 
9.58.b
Packet Pg. 229
Attachment: Melissa Peeker Agreement  (2025-568 : Sets Terms & Conditions of Employment for a Payroll Supervisor)
 
 
Page 4 of 9 
which she will be paid in the next fiscal year. If the employee does not comply with t his 
requirement, then the employee will not be eligible for any accrued time buyout in the next fiscal 
year.”  
 
ARTICLE V 
 
SICK LEAVE 
 
1.  Sick leave is absence necessitated by Peeker’s illness or other physical disability.  Sick 
leave will be accumulated at the rate of one and one-quarter (1 1/4) days per month or (fifteen [15] 
days per year), total accumulated sick leave of three hundred (300) days.  After three hundred (300) 
days, additional paid sick leave may be granted in the sole discretion of the Town Board.  In order to 
receive sick leave,  Peeker shall, when absent because of sickness for more than three (3) days, 
furnish the Supervisor, when requested by him/her, with a medical certificate.  Failure to furnish a 
medical certificate will result in loss of pay for absent days.  The Town Board, in its discretion, may 
request a physical examination of Peeker before her return to work. 
 
2.  Peeker, or her legal representative, upon retirement or severance, is en titled to cash 
payment for accumulated sick leave.  Said payment shall be paid in a lump sum the value of her 
accumulated and unused sick leave to the extent of one hundred (100%) percent of the first two 
hundred and eighty (280) days thereof. 
 
3. The parties mutually agree that excessive absenteeism due to abuse of sick leave should 
be discouraged. Therefore, the Town may request a doctor's certificate from chronic abusers of 
sick leave (e.g., numerous illness absences even though Peeker has accumulated sick leave),  
regardless of the length of the illness.  Submitting a claim based on a false statement, or covering a 
period during which the employee was not actually disabled, will be considered as abusing the 
sick leave provision. E m p l o y e es  who abuse the sick leave provision shall be subject to 
disciplinary action. 
 
4. Peeker may elect to reduce the sick time accrued under paragraph "1" one by filing a 
written election with the Supervisor one (1) month prior to payment.  Buy-out shall be in lots of 
ten (10) sick days. No buy-out shall be permitted unless at the time of election Peeker has 
accumulated at least fifty (50) sick days. The rate of pay and payment method will be the same as 
outlined in the 2021-2026 Superior Officer’s Contract, Article XI Section C. 
 
ARTICLE VI 
 
GRIEVANCE PROCEDURE 
 
1.  Consideration of Grievance. 
 
A grievance by Peeker shall be made, in writing, to the Town Board.  Upon receipt of the 
grievance, the Town Board may request Peeker to submit any agreed statement of facts or her 
9.58.b
Packet Pg. 230
Attachment: Melissa Peeker Agreement  (2025-568 : Sets Terms & Conditions of Employment for a Payroll Supervisor)
 
 
Page 5 of 9 
version of the facts, or any other documents that the Town Board may deem pertinent to the 
determination of the appeal. 
 
The Town Board shall conduct a hearing within twenty (20) business days of receipt of an 
appeal.  Within twenty (20) business days after the hearing, the Town Board shall make a decision 
based on its findings and advise  Peeker.  The decision of the Town Board shall be final and all 
parties bound thereby. 
 
2.  Time of Hearings. 
 
All discussions and hearings shall, so far as practicable, be conducted during working hours. 
 
3.  Representation. 
 
Peeker shall have the right at all times to representation of her choosing. 
 
4.  Limitations. 
 
If a grievance occurs and cannot be resolved immediately, Peeker shall obey all directives 
and shall present the grievance as soon thereafter as practicable.  Grievances which are not presented 
within ten (10) days of the occurrence shall be deemed to have been abandoned. 
 
5.  Withdrawn Grievances. 
 
Peeker may withdraw a grievance at any point in the grievance procedure. 
 
 
ARTICLE VII 
 
PENSION AND LONGEVITY 
 
Peeker represents that she is a member of the New York State Employees Retirement 
System.  As a Tier IV member, Peeker is a participant in the Article 14 or Article 15 Coordinated 
Retirement Plan. 
 
Longevity payments shall be based on the present year’s salary and the percentages shall be 
taken there from.  Peeker shall be paid longevity based on the following schedule: 
 
Four percent (4%) of base pay after ten (10) years of service. 
Six percent (6%) of base pay after fifteen (15) years of service. 
Seven percent (7%) of base pay after eighteen (18) years of service. 
 
It is agreed by and between the parties that Peeker’s prior service with the Town shall be 
credited in determining longevity pay.

Packet Pg. 231
Attachment: Melissa Peeker Agreement  (2025-568 : Sets Terms & Conditions of Employment for a Payroll Supervisor)
 
 
Page 6 of 9 
 
ARTICLE VIII 
 
HEALTH INSURANCE 
 
1.  The Town shall pay, on Peeker’s behalf, one hundred (100%) percent of the cost of either 
the individual or family coverage for hospitalization under the Town Health Insurance Program.  The 
Town shall pay for one hundred (100%) percent coverage for Peeker if she retires from the Town 
and the Town shall also pay to the extent of fifty (50%) percent coverage on the premiums for her 
family. 
 
If Peeker and her spouse, if employed through the Town, are  currently receiving (or are 
eligible to receive) family health benefits through the Town, only one will be permitted to continue 
to receive family level coverage.  In this event, the person whose coverage changes from family to 
individual or no coverage will be entitled to the health insurance buy-out, provided that he/she:  (1) 
has submitted to the Town documentation showing that he/she has health insurance coverage other 
than through the New York State Health Insurance Plan (NYSHIP); and (b) remains in changed 
status for a period of 12 consecutive months.  The 12-month period will coincide with the annual 
option transfer period.   Payment will be made annually during the June or December first following 
the end of the 12-month period, provided that Peeker or her spouse remains in the changed status. 
Peeker may reinstate coverage within the 12-month period if he/she experiences a qualifying event 
and has submitted to the Town adequate documentation of that event, consistent with the rules and 
regulations of the Town’s health insurance plan and applicable laws and regulations.   
 
At retirement, the former employee who is otherwise eligible for family retiree health 
insurance coverage through the Town but for the operation of t his provision shall continue to be 
ineligible for family retiree health insurance coverage through the Town.  However, during 
retirement, the former employee may reinstate her/her own family health insurance coverage, if the 
former employee has dependents as defined in the Plan, in the event of an emergency causing the 
loss of the other person’s Town health insurance, consistent with the rules and regulations of the 
Town’s health insurance plan and applicable laws and regulations. 
 
In the event that Peeker’s employment with the Town should terminate, she shall have the 
option, at her own expense, to participate in the Town Health Insurance Program, consistent with 
applicable laws, rules and regulations.   
 
The service requirement for receipt of health insurance in retirement shall be ten  
consecutive years of service with the Town. However, if Peeker leaves Town service she 
must continue with NYSHIP in vested status by paying the entire cost of coverage, or by being 
enrolled as an e m p l o y e e at a subsequent participating agency or by being enrolled as a 
dependent on a NYSHIP policy in order to retain eligibility for retiree health benefits through 
the Town. If  Peeker leaves to work for another NYSHIP employer, she is not eligible for retiree 
health insurance if she vests with the second employer 
 
9.58.b
Packet Pg. 232
Attachment: Melissa Peeker Agreement  (2025-568 : Sets Terms & Conditions of Employment for a Payroll Supervisor)
 
 
Page 7 of 9 
2.  The Town shall pay, on Peeker’s behalf, one hundred (100%) percent of the cost of either 
the individual or family plan for dental coverage under the Riverhead Town Dental Plan.  If  Peeker 
and her spouse, if employed through the Town, are currently receiving (or are eligible to receive) 
family dental insurance benefits through the Town, only one will be permitted to continue to receive 
family level coverage.  In this event, the person whose coverage changes from family to individual 
coverage or no coverage will be entitled to the dental insurance buy-out.  Should that person choose 
to decline to receive individual coverage, then that person will be eligible for the buy -out of the 
individual coverage. 
 
3.  The Town shall pay, on Peeker’s behalf, one hundred (100%) percent of the cost of either 
the individual or family plan for optical coverage under the Riverhead Town Optical Plan.  If  Peeker 
and her spouse, if employed through the Town, are currently receiving (or are eligible to receive) 
family optical insurance benefits through the Town, only one will be permitted to continue to receive 
family level coverage.  In this event, the person whose coverage changes from family to individual 
coverage or no coverage will be entitled to the optical insurance buy-out.  Should that person choose 
to decline to receive individual coverage, then that person will be eligible for the buy -out of the 
individual coverage. 
 
4.  The Town will insure Peeker’s life in accordance with the maximum death benefit 
provided by the Employees Retirement System for Tier IV members.   
 
  5. Peeker, at her option, may elect not to accept the Town's hospitalization coverage for 
a period of not less than one calendar year and receive the following payment during the first full 
pay period of each year the election is made: $1,650 if Peeker changes from family to no 
coverage; $900 if Peeker changes from family to individual coverage; $750 if Peeker changes 
from individual to no coverage. Also, at her option, Peeker may elect not to accept the dental 
coverage for a period of not less than one calendar year and receive the following payment 
during the first full pay period of each year the election is made:  $230 if Peeker changes from 
family to no coverage; $150 if Peeker changes from family to individual coverage; $80 if Peeker 
changes from individual to no coverage. Also, at her option, Peeker may elect not to accept the 
optical coverage for a period of not less than one calendar year and receive a payment of twenty 
five dollars ($25.00) during the first full pay period of each year the election is made.  Peeker 
must sign an application form each year and said application shall include an acknowledgment 
that he is covered under another plan 
  
 ARTICLE IX 
 
 GENERAL PROVISIONS 
 
1.  The Town agrees to provide legal counsel to defend Peeker in any action arising out of an 
assault on Peeker on Town business, and the Town hereby agrees to defend, indemnify, and hold  
Peeker harmless for any and all acts performed for the Town, its agents and employees, including 
but not limited to preparation, certification and sealing of plans prepared exclusively for the Town, 
its agents and employees, provided Peeker was acting within the scope of her employment.  In the 
9.58.b
Packet Pg. 233
Attachment: Melissa Peeker Agreement  (2025-568 : Sets Terms & Conditions of Employment for a Payroll Supervisor)
 
 
Page 8 of 9 
event that Peeker is appointed, authorized or directed by the Town or one of its agencies to represent 
it as a member of the board of directors of an organization or agency, then she shall be covered by 
the provisions of Public Officers Law Section 18 and Town Code Sections 15-1 and 15-2 pertaining 
to the defense and indemnification of officers and employees of public entities, provided Peeker is 
otherwise eligible for coverage pursuant to the terms of those provisions. 
 
2.  If Peeker is injured or assaulted in the course of employment, she shall receive 100% of 
her salary for the first six months during which she is absent from work, and 85% of her salary for 
any time beyond that period, until such time as her application for reinstatement to full duty status, 
or, in the event of permanent disability, her application for a disability pension be finally determined 
or by a physician's examination determining no further disability, whichever comes first.  If  Peeker 
is injured on the job and reports the same to the Supervisor, and has to be absent from work, no days 
shall be deducted from her sick leave for such injury.  If Peeker receives a compensation check for 
lost time due to a compensable injury, she shall endorse her check over to the Town.  The above 
shall apply if Peeker was acting within the scope of her employment.  Nothing contained herein shall 
in any way be deemed to restrict the Town’s right to separate Peeker pursuant to the provisions of 
Civil Service Law Sections 71-73. 
 
3.  A leave of absence, without pay, may be granted to Peeker in the discretion of the Town 
Board for a maximum of six (6) months, upon written application therefore and good cause shown. 
 
4.  If Peeker is absent without leave or without due notification to the Supervisor, she shall 
suffer loss of pay for the days of such absence.  
 
5.  Peeker will be paid every two (2) weeks on second Thursday after the pay-period end.   
 
6.  Upon Peeker’s request to examine her official employment personnel file, she may be 
permitted to do so at the discretion of the Town Board.  Any material classified as confidential shall 
not be subject to duplication by Peeker, but she shall have an opportunity to read said material and 
make a written reply, which shall be inserted in her personnel folder. 
 
7.  To the extent permitted by the U.S. Internal Revenue Code and the New York State 
Income Tax Laws, the Town shall permit employee to establish a deferred compensation plan for 
said employee. 
 
8.  The Town will provide a college and post -graduate incentive program for courses 
approved by the Town Board.  The Town will reimburse Peeker the tuition cost on a grade related 
basis.  A grade of "A" will receive seventy-five (75%) percent of the tuition cost.  A grade of "B" 
will receive fifty (50%) percent of the tuition cost.  A grade of "C" will receive twenty-five (25%) 
percent of the tuition cost.  Payment will only be made upon submission of voucher and proof of 
grade.

 ARTICLE X 
 
 WAGES 
 
Peeker shall receive the following annual salary: January 1 through December 31 each year: 
$98,000.00. This salary shall be pro-rated in the year 2025 with an effective date commencing June 
15, 2025.  
 
Effective January 1, 2026, Peekers’s salary will be increased annually based on the consumer 
price index for New York, Northern New Jersey, and Long Island limited and not to exceed 3.5% or 
equal to the CSEA salary and Step increases, whichever is greater. 
 
    Peeker’s base salary for each remaining year of this Agreement shall not be less than that of 
the preceding year.

06.17.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-569 
 
RATIFIES RESOLUTION FOR HOME RULE REQUEST IN SUPPORT OF BILL 
(SENATE BILL #S.8378-B/ASSEMBLY BILL #A.8809-B) FOR “AN ACT TO AMEND 
CHAPTER 495 OF THE LAWS OF 2011 RELATING TO THE CONVEYANCE OF 
LAND FORMERLY USED AS AN ARMORY TO THE TOWN OF RIVERHEAD, 
COUNTY OF SUFFOLK IN RELATION TO THE USE OF SUCH PROPERTY” 
 
Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
WHEREAS, New York State Bill S04404/A06825, entitled “Relates to the 
conveyance of land formerly used as an armory to the town of Riverhead in the county 
of Suffolk”, signed into law by the Governor on August 31, 2022 (Laws of the State of 
New York 2011, Chapter 495), transferred the 5.72-acre former New York State Armory 
facility, including a structure of approximately 32,101 square feet to the Town of  
Riverhead in 2011; and  
   
WHEREAS, despite various attempts, the Town of Riverhead has been unable to 
repurpose the former Armory for improvement and use by the police department, justice 
court, public safety and/or recreational programs developed and operated by the 
Riverhead Police Department as set forth in the enabling state legislation; and 
 
WHEREAS, YMCA of Long Island leaders have toured the Armory site with 
Town of Riverhead staff and expressed interest in leasing the Armory site from the 
Town for a variety of uses all centered and focused on well-being, including but not 
limited to, fitness and health, education, designed for and spanning ages from pre-
school/early childhood, children, pre-teen and teen programs, adults and older adults for 
local and county residents; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Town of Riverhead seeks to propose a ninety-nine (99) year 
lease with the YMCA of Long Island for consideration in the amount of $1.00.  
 
WHEREAS, Bill S.8378A/B.8809B has been introduced in the New York State 
Senate and in the New York State Assembly with the intent to Amend Chapter 495 of 
the Laws of 2011 relating to the conveyance of land formerly used as an armory to the 
Town of Riverhead, County of Suffolk in relation to the use of such property; and  
 
WHEREAS, a Home Rule request has been received by the Town of Riverhead 
from State Assemblywoman Jodi Giglio in support of the above captioned legislation. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Town Board of the Town of 
Riverhead hereby ratifies the support of the efforts of the New York State Legislature 
and approves a Home Rule request for Bill S.8378A/B.8809B for “an act to Amend 
Chapter 495 of the laws of 2011 relating to the conveyance of land formerly used as an 
9.59
Packet Pg. 236
armory to the Town of Riverhead, County of Suffolk in relation to the use of such 
property”; and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, that the Supervisor and the Town Clerk, are authorized to execute 
the Home Rule Request in support of this proposed State legislation and such Home 
Rule Request shall be delivered to the Senate and Assembly Post Offices, and, be it 
further,  
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be and is hereby authorized to forward a copy 
of this resolution to the Office of the Town Attorney, and State Assemblywoman Jodi 
Giglio giglioj2@nyassembly.gov and State Senator Anthony Palumbo 
palumbo@nysenate.gov; and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.   
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
SECONDER: Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD  
NOTICE OF PUBLIC HEARING  
 
 PLEASE TAKE NOTICE that a public hearing will be held before the Town Board of the 
Town of Riverhead at Riverhead Town Hall, 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, New York, on the 
1st day of July, 2025 at or about 2:20 p.m. to amend Chapter 289 of the Riverhead Town Code 
Titled “Vehicles, Traffic and Parking Regulations” Article IV Section 10 thereof titled, “Parking 
Prohibited”  
The intent of the proposed legislation is to remediate a dangerous condition caused by 
the parking of vehicles upon Youngs Avenue. 
 
 A copy of the entire text of the proposed local law and the provisions of the existing law to 
be amended may be reviewed at the Office of the Town Clerk, 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, 
New York 11901, between the hours of 8:30 a.m. and 4:30 p.m., Monday through Friday and can 
be accessed on the Town of Riverhead website at: www.townofriverheadny.gov under the Agenda 
and Minutes for the June 17, 2025 Town Board Meeting. 
Dated:  Riverhead, New York 
  June 17, 2025 
 
 
 BY THE ORDER OF THE TOWN BOARD 
 OF THE TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 JAMES M. WOOTEN, Town Clerk

06.17.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-571 
 
GRANTS FINAL SITE PLAN APPROVAL FOR THE SITE PLAN AMENDMENT 
APPLICATION OF ISLAND WATER PARK (D/B/A SCOTT'S POINTE) 5835 MIDDLE 
COUNTRY  ROAD, CALVERTON, NY SCTM NO. 600-135-1-7.34 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Town Board is in receipt of a site plan application 
seeking to amend the previously approved site plan of Island Water Park (d/b/a Scott’s 
Pointe); and  
 
WHEREAS, proposed amendments include legalization of a go -kart track, 
pickleball courts, and conversion of an existing interior storage space for use as a 
catering/event space; and  
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2024-996, adopted December 17, 2024, the Town 
Board classified the action as an Unlisted action pursuant to SEQRA, and commenced 
coordinated review among involved agencies; and  
 
 WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2024 -1009, adopted January 7, 2025, the Town 
Board scheduled a public hearing on the site plan application; and  
 
 WHEREAS, a public hearing was held on January 22, 2025, at 4 W. 2 nd Street, 
Riverhead, NY, at 6:00 o’clock p.m., at which time all those who wished to speak on the 
application were afforded an opportunity to do so; and  
 
 WHEREAS¸ the public hearing was closed on January 22, 2025, with the record 
being left open for the submission of written comments for 10 days, until January 31, 
2025; and  
 
 WHEREAS¸ by Resolution No. 2025 -234, dated March 4, 2025, the Town Board 
issued a Conditional Negative Declaration (CND) pursuant to SEQRA, finding that the 
proposed action is not anticipated to result in any significant negative environmental 
impacts, with the imposition of certain conditions; and  
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2025 -460, adopted May 21, 2025, the Town 
Board granted preliminary site plan approval for the application, subject to the following 
conditions being satisfied prior to final site plan approval: 
 
2. The applicant must obtain a Freshwater Wetlands Jurisdictional 
Determination from the NYSDEC. 
 
9.61
Packet Pg. 251
3. The applicant must fully reclaim the mine under NYSDEC Permit ID 1 -4730-
01022/00002, and provide certification to the Town of Riverhead that the mine 
has been closed out. 
 
4. The applicant shall satisfy the Chief Fire Marshal’s comments from letter 
dated February 25, 2025. 
 
5. The site plan shall be amended to include a barrier around the outside of the 
track to control stormwater management and erosion into the lake, as detailed 
in the Town Engineer’s May 14, 2025 memo. 
 
6. The applicant must resolve any outstanding violations with the NYSDEC 
relative to the site improvements which were made without benefit of a permit 
from the NYSDEC.  
 
7. The applicant shall file a covenant on the property, in a form approved by the 
Town Attorney, restricting the use of the track to go -karts, and that use of the 
track for any other type of vehicles shall be prohibited; and  
 
WHEREAS, the applicant has addressed the conditions of preliminary site plan 
as follows: 
 
1. Applicant has entered into an Order on Consent with the New York State 
Department of Environmental Conservation, DEC No. R1 -2041109-179, 
dated June 13, 202 5, which assessed penalties, provides a compliance 
schedule for reclamation of the mining site, and, until fully remediated in 
accordance with the Order, considers all violations described in the DEC 
complaint as “continuing violations,” which the DEC shall not institute any 
action or proceeding for penalties or other relief described, for so long as 
Respondent (applicant) remains in compliance with the Order.  The Town 
considers this Order to have adequately addressed condition Nos.   3 and 6 of 
the preliminary site plan approval. 
 
2. The applicant has provided an email response from Kevin Jennings of the 
NYSDEC, dated June 13, 2025, which states that “activities that took place 
before 1/1/25 would not have needed a Freshwater Wetlands Permit at your 
site.”  The Town considers this email as adequately addressing condition No. 
2 of the preliminary site plan approval, with the caveat that if the NYSDEC 
requires further review and approval under Freshwater Wetlands regulations, 
the applicant must abide by same. 
 
3. The applicant has obtained Fire Marshal permits, Permit Nos. 25 -0063 and 
25-0018, necessary for the proposed site plan.  Upon final inspections by the 
Town Fire Marshal, these permits and corresponding Certificates of 
Compliance will satisfy condition No. 4 of the preliminary site plan approval. 
 
4. The applicant has filed a Covenant and Restriction, in a form approved by the 
Town Attorney’s office, on June 16, 2025 under Liber D00013298, Page 163, 
which satisfies condition No. 7 of the preliminary site plan approval. 
 
5. The Town Engineer reviewed a grading and drainage plan relevant , prepared 
by A.M. Weber  to the go -kart track, and in a memo dated June 16, 2025, 
9.61
Packet Pg. 252
stated that the AM Weber drainage plans adequately addressed his concerns 
about drainage on the track and erosion along the perimeter of the track , 
which satisfies condition No. 5 of the preliminary site plan approval; and  
 
WHEREAS, the applicant paid the necessary Key Money, as required by the 
Riverhead Water District, on June 16, 2025; and  
 
WHEREAS, the Town Board has considered the preliminary site plan approval 
resolution, including the conditions therein imposed.  Now, therefore be it 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Board hereby grants final approval for the Island 
Water Park Amended Site Plan application, including a site plan, prepared and stamped 
by James R. Holzmacher, PE, dated April 10, 2025, with sheets labeled C -1: Existing 
Site Plan, C -2: Proposed Site Plan, C -3: Parking Layout Plan and Calcs, C -4: Grading 
and Drainage Plan, C4.1: Existing Pickleball and Go -Kart Topo Plan, C -5: Lighting & 
Landscape Plan, subject to the following conditions:  
 
1. That the provisions of the Riverhead Town Code which are not addressed by 
this resolution, or other official action of the Town shall, at all times, be 
complied with by the owner of the property covered by this site plan.  
 
2. That the form, design, location, and color of all signage shall be submitted for 
a sign permit prior to being installed at the property, and that all signage so 
proposed shall be coordinated in appearance and design, and that all 
provisions of Article XLVIII of the Riverhead Town Code shall be complied 
with, and that all tenants shall be apprised of said requirements as well as 
any restrictions imposed as a condition of site plan approval granted herein. 
 
3. That any outdoor lighting shall be installed pursuant to Article XLIX of the 
Town Code, and that no lighting shall be adjusted in such a way as to cause 
direct glare on neighboring properties or adjoining highways, and that all site 
lighting shall be maintained in good working order. 
 
4. That the applicant is familiar with Town Code Chapter 251 entitled, “Noise, 
Public Nuisances, and Property Maintenance,” and Chapter 245, prohibiting 
the accumulation of litter, and requiring the enclosure of dumpsters, and 
agrees to abide by the same. 
 
5. That parking, paving, and drainage shall be provided and maintained 
pursuant to specifications outlined in Town Code §301-231. 
 
6. That any and all landscaped and paved areas shall be regularly maintained in 
an orderly and professional manner and kept free of weeds and litter, and that 
any planters, planter boxes, window boxes or other container plantings shall 
be likewise maintained on a year-round basis. 
 
7. That the applicant shall satisfy all requirements of the Building and Fire Code 
of New York State; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that prior to the issuance of a Building Permit, the following 
conditions shall be satisfied: 
 
9.61
Packet Pg. 253
1. The Town Supervisor, or their assign, signs one (1) mylar and six (6) paper 
copies of the site plan drawings.  Prior to signature of the plans, the plans 
shall be revised as follows: 
 
a. Sheet C -4 of the site plan shall be revised to show the drainage 
structures installed per the A.M. Weber drainage plan.  
 
RESOLVED, that no temporary or permanent Certificates of Occupancy shall 
issue until the following conditions are satisfied: 
 
1. The applicant applies for all necessary inspections as required by Town Code 
§301-305F. 
 
2. The applicant passes any necessary inspections from the Riverhead Building 
Department and Fire Marshal’s office; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that pursuant to Town Code §301 -303F, this final approval shall be 
valid for 36 months from the date of approval with the possibility of one 12 -month 
extension by the Town Board, upon a request of the applicant in writing made at least 
30 days prior to the expiration of the original 36 month period; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to forward a certified copy 
of this resolution to the Ken Myers ( ken@scottspointe.com), the Building Department, 
the Town Attorney’s office; and be it further 
 
 RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified copy of same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.  
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [4 TO 1] 
MOVER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
SECONDER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
AYES: Tim Hubbard, Kenneth Rothwell, Robert Kern, Joann Waski 
NAYS: Denise Merrifield

AUTHORIZES THE SUPERVISOR TO EXECUTE AN AGREEMENT WITH THE 
RIVERHEAD BUSINESS IMPROVEMENT DISTRICT MANAGEMENT ASSOCIATION, 
INC. REGARDING 2025 CALENDAR YEAR EVENTS 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
WHEREAS, the Town of Riverhead, with the assistance of the Riverhead 
Business Improvement District Management Association, Inc. (BIDMA), wishes to 
continue to administer the District Plan as adopted by the Town of Riverhead pursuant 
to Local Law No. 222 of 1991, during the 2025 calendar year. 
 
WHEREAS, BIDMA has identified certain events activities/promotions, 
sponsorships and services more fully delineated in the attached agreement. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Town Supervisor is authorized 
to execute an agreement in substantially the form attached with the Riverhead Business 
Improvement District Management Association, Inc. regarding 2025 calendar year 
BIDMA operations; and be it further,  
 
RESOLVED, co-sponsorship and approval of the 2025 calendar year events and 
services are subject to and contingent upon any subsequent restrictions, limitations, and 
parameters that may be imposed pursuant to New York State Executive Orders, as 
amended and/or modified, as well any and all other pertinent laws, rules or regulations, 
as amended and/or modified are imposed subsequent hereto and be it further,  
 
RESOLVED, that the Town of Riverhead Accounting Department is authorized to 
modify the budget for Fund CM1 Business Improvement District to conform to BIDMA’s 
2025 Budget; and be it further,  
 
RESOLVED, that a copy of this resolution shall be forwarded to  the Accounting 
Department and the Office of the Town Attorney; and be it further,  
  
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.   
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
SECONDER: Robert Kern, Councilman

Agreement 
 
made between the 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
(Business Improvement District) 
 
-and- 
 
RIVERHEAD BUSINESS IMPROVEMENT DISTRICT 
MANAGEMENT ASSOCIATION, INC. 
 
This Agreement deemed effective the     day of            , 2025, between the Town of 
Riverhead Business Improvement District (“ BID”), with principal offices located at 4 
West Second Street, Riverhead, New York, 11901,  and the Riverhead Business 
Improvement District Management Association, Inc. (“BIDMA”), a not -for-profit 
corporation organized under the laws of the State of New York, having its principal 
offices at 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, New York, 11901. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, the parties mutually agree that: 
   
1. The BIDMA shall offer projects, capital improvements, events and services 
related to the BID which are attached hereto as Schedule “A”.  The calendar 
year 20 24 projects/events/services delineated in the attached Schedule “A” 
shall be deemed co -sponsored if so delineated as same by both the BID and 
BIDMA and are hereby approved .  However, the BID reserves the unilateral 
right to require BIDMA to procure additional liability insurance, even in regard 
to co-sponsored events.  BIDMA agrees to timely apply for, obtain approval 
and comply with all applicable Riverhead Town Code Chapter 255 conditions.  
BID, as a co -sponsor of such events, shall waive Chapter 255 permit fees 
regarding BIDMA’s Chapter 255 applications as well as the time restrictions .  
The BIDMA will file applicable applications for special event permits , ie. 
Assembly Permits, Fireworks Permits, Show mobile Permit and any and all 
Suffolk County Department of Health and New York State Liquor Authority 
permits, if necessary. 
 
2. The BIDMA is exempt from the insurance requirement, as the Town of 
Riverhead is a co -sponsor and holds the liability insurance .  For -profit 
vendors contracted for events are required to obtain and render a Certificate 
of Liability insurance and a separate primary and non -contributory 
endorsement letter listing the Town of Riverhead, Riverhead Business 
Improvement District and Riverhead Business Improvement District 
Management Association; vendor liability insurance must meet the criteria 
required by Chapter 255 of the Riverhead Town Code .  Any and all for -profit 
vendors are required to submit a signed Town of Riverhead license 
agreement and are required to complete and sign a hold harmless 
participation agreement in place of liability insurance, listing the Town, BID 
and BIDMA as being held safe and harmless from liability arising from 
vendor’s actions. 
9.65.a
Packet Pg. 273
Attachment: BID and BIDMA 2025 Agreement  (2025-575 : Authorizes the Supervisor to Execute an Agreement with the Riverhead Bidma 2025)
 
2 
 
 
3. BID shall provide all proper and re asonable funding regarding administrative 
services/expenses incurred by the BIDMA necessary to carry out the District 
Plan as adopted by the Town of Riverhead pursuant to Local Law #222 of 
1991.  Administrative services as specified herein are defined as  payment of 
employee salaries and the associated payroll expenses, rent, purchase of 
incidental office supplies , telephone expenses, photocopier expenses, 
insurance and advertising expenses  and any other expenses related to the 
actual administration of the BID .  The BIDMA shall provide a detailed, 
comprehensive and exhaustive accounting of all actual and anticipated 
administrative services/expenses it has or anticipates it shall incur during the 
term of this Agreement prior to execution of this Agreement.  The BID shall 
pay all legitimate, proper and necessary administrative expenses in a timely 
manner as addressed in Schedule A .  The BIDMA agrees to provide all 
documentation, written, recorded or otherwise in support of its determination 
of administrative services/expenses to the Chief Financial Administrator on a 
monthly basis and to any member of the Town Attorney’s Office, if requested, 
within three business days, or if not available, within a reasonable time.  
 
4. The BIDMA shall proffer and recommend to the BID , Town Board designated 
projects, including capital improvements, events and services designed for 
the purpose of promoting and enhancing the business improvement district in 
the int erests of economic stimulus and/or betterment of the district as a 
whole. 
 
5.  The BIDMA shall submit a written list of projects, including suggested capital 
improvements, events and services , including actual or estimated costs with 
supporting documentation and projected dates of commencement/completion  
it recommends for approval to the BID on or before September 1st for those 
projects, events and services antic ipated to occur on or after January 1 st of 
the following calendar year.  In addition, the BIDMA shall submit its budgetary 
request regarding its recommended list of projects, including capital 
improvements, events and services, as well as its projected administrative 
expenses to the Town of Riverhead’s Chief Financial Officer on or before 
September 1st.  The recommendations of the BIDMA are not binding upon the 
BID-Town Board  which may approve or  disapprove any or all of the 
recommendations.  For those projects, events or services that the BIDMA 
wishes to recommend and becomes aware of after October 1 st, the BIDMA 
shall forthwith notify the BID of its recommendation  in the same format 
addressed above .  The BIDMA shall and must provide a valid and properly 
authorized written BIDMA resolution by its board approving the recommended 
projects, capital improvements, events, services, costs and budget allocations 
before the BID shall consider same for approval. 
 
6. Notification Procedure of recommended projects, events or services. 
 
 The BIDMA shall notify the BID of all recommended projects, events or 
services by submitting in writing to each town board member a list of 
recommended projects, events, or services so recommended.  The BID shall 
9.65.a
Packet Pg. 274
Attachment: BID and BIDMA 2025 Agreement  (2025-575 : Authorizes the Supervisor to Execute an Agreement with the Riverhead Bidma 2025)
 
3 
 
consider and address each of the recommended projects, events or services 
in work session  and notify BIDMA of its decision in a timely manner .  The 
BIDMA shall make available to the BID one or more persons who are familiar 
with the recommended projects, events  or services whom shall be present at 
the scheduled work session.  Said representative shall be made available for 
any subsequent meetings of the BID on an as -needed basis.  The BID shall 
consider each recommended project, event or service and the anticipated 
cost of same.  For those projects, events or services so approved by the BID, 
the BID shall provide the necessary funding to the BIDMA in a timely manner .  
The BID reserves the right to request additional information and/or 
documentation at any time and may withhold partial or full payment in the 
absence of same. 
 
7.   Location of Meetings.   
 
 All BIDMA meetings shall take place at the Riverhead Town Hall board 
meeting room  at dates and times to be determined by the parties to this 
agreement.  All monthly meeting dates shall be provided in writing to each 
town board member and the town attorney’s office no later than 30 days 
before any scheduled meeting , including all special meetings .  In the event 
that the BIDMA schedules all of its monthly meetings before the subject 
calendar year, a schedule of same shall be provided  to each town board 
member and the town attorney’s office within 10 days of publication.   
 
8. Minutes/Agenda of Meetings. 
 
 The BI DMA secretary or designee shall keep an accurate record of all 
business that comes before the BIDMA, including but not limited to: subject 
matter, identification of all parties at the meetings  (including directors, officers 
and members and nature of participation) and resolutions, including resolution 
number and identification of voting interests.  An accurate record of all 
business that comes before the BIDMA shall  be provided to the BID -Town 
Board, Town Attorney’s Office and the Chief Financial Officer within seven (7) 
days of the subject meeting. 
 
9. Attendees at Meetings. 
 
   The BID and BIDMA hereby acknowledge and agree that every meeting shall 
be open to the general publi c, except that an executive session of such 
association may be called and business transacted thereat in accordance 
with the New York State Public Officers Law §105. 
 
10. Assignment 
 
This Agreement may not be assigned by the BIDMA without the express 
written consent of the Town of Riverhead Business Improvement District.

 11. Term of the Agreement.  
 
     The term of this Agreement shall be deemed to have commenced on January 
1, 2025, and expire on December 31, 2025, and shall not b e renewed except 
upon the written consent of all parties. 
 
12.  Records. 
 
The BIDMA further agrees to provide any and all documents , records, notes, 
or other information regarding all recommended projects, events or services 
regarding the business improvement district  immediately upon request by the 
BID-Town Board, Town’s Financial Administrator and/or Chief Fiscal Officer  
and any employee of the Town Attorney’s Office, or anyone so designated by 
the above parties to receive same within three (3) days of such request.  
 
13.  Insurance 
 
The BIDMA shall procure insurance in amounts and at policy limits as may 
be determined by the BID notwithstanding any other insurance requirements 
or obligations pursuant to New York State Law. 
 
14.  Director/Officer Elections 
 
The BIDMA shall notify the BID of all candidates for director and officer 
positions in writing no later than ten (10) days before the respective election 
regarding the respective classification and position ; for example, commercial 
property owner or commercial tenant and/or officer position and the subject 
term.  The BIDMA shall notify the BID in writing of all election results within 
three (3) days of the election, including classification, title and term of office. 
 
15.  Independent Contractor 
 
Notwithstanding anything contained herein to the contrary, it is specifically 
understood and agreed that, in the performance of the terms, covenants and 
conditions of the Agreement, neither the BIDMA nor any of its officers, 
directors, employees, agents or independent contractors shall be deemed to 
be acting as agents, servants, or employees of the Town by virtue of this 
Agreement or by virtue of any approval, permit, license, grant, right or other 
authorization given by the Town of any of its officers, agents or employees 
pursuant to this Agreement, but shall be deemed to be independent 
contractors performing services for the BID or the BIDMA, as the case may 
be, without power or authority to bind the Town and shall be deemed solely 
responsible for all acts taken or omitted by them in the performance of or 
otherwise pursuant to this Agreement.   
 
 16.  Indemnification 
 
(a)  Except as otherwise expressly stated herein, the BIDMA hereby assumes 
liability for, and hereby agrees to indemnify, protect, defend, save and hold

harmless, the BID-Town from and against any and all liabilities, obligations, 
losses, damages, penalties, claims, actions, suits, costs, expenses and 
disbursements, including, without limitations, reasonable legal and 
investigative fees and expenses, of whatsoever kind and nature (hereinafter 
called “Liabilities”) which may be incurred or imposed at any time (whether 
during the Agreement Term or thereafter) on the BID-Town (whether or not 
also indemnified against by any other person) and in any way relating to or 
arising out of, or alleged (by a person other than the BID-Town) to in any way

without limitations, the following:  claims or penalties arising from any violation 
of any federal, state or local laws, rules or regulations or insurance 
requirements, as well as any claim resulting from latent, patent, and other

copyright infringement, any tort claim or claim for damages , any claim or 
liability in respect to any adverse environmental impact or effects. The BIDMA

such liability, and the BID-Town shall cooperate with the BIDMA by providing,

(i) the BID-Town shall be consulted as to the legal counsel to be employed in

BIDMA notice that, in good faith judgment, an important general interest of 
the BID-Town is involved in such liability or potential liability, the BID-Town 
shall have the right to consult with the BIDMA in the defense against or 
settlement of such liability.   
 
(b) The BIDMA shall require each of its contractors and subcontractors to agree 
to indemnify the Town and assume liability for injuries on the same basis as 
the BIDMA under subsection (a) above.   
 
(c) The obligations of the BIDMA under this section shall survive the expiration or 
earlier termination of this Agreement and are expressly made for the benefit 
of, and shall be enforceable by the Town without necessity of declaring this 
Agreement in default.

19.  Alcohol-Related Events 
 
BIDMA acknowledges, understands and agrees, to the following conditions 
regarding any event delineated in the attached Schedule A, or amendments 
thereto, whereby alcohol shall be sold, served or consumed: 
  
(a) BIDMA shall require each alcohol vendor participating in the event , defined 
as any party or entity selling, or serving or providing alcohol for consumption, to 
provide sufficient insurance liability coverage, based upon the number of 
participants or attendees in the event , which shall be subject to approval by the 
Town Attorney’s Office and its Insurance Administrator, in its discretion.  BIDMA 
shall also require each alcohol vendor to comply with the Town of 
Riverhead Alcohol Policy. 
 
(b) The BID, specifically, The Town of Riverhead, and BIDMA, shall be named in 
all certificates of liability insurance coverage, as additional insureds , regarding 
alcohol coverage, with proper endorsement. 
 
(c) The certificate of insurance must be provided to the Town Attorney’s Office 
not later than fourteen (14) days before the scheduled event.   The Town 
reserves the right to require additional insurance coverage it so deems in its 
best interests.

 This Agreement contains all the terms and conditions agreed upon by the parties 
 hereto and no other agreement, oral or otherwise, regarding the subject matter o f

 In the event any covenant, condition or provision contained herein is held to be

Attachment: 2025 BIDMA Budget FINAL  (2025-575 : Authorizes the Supervisor to Execute an Agreement with the Riverhead Bidma 2025)
 
06.17.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-576 
 
AUTHORIZES THE RIVERHEAD POLICE DEPARTMENT TO APPLY FOR GRANT 
FROM USDOJ FOR BODY CAMERAS SOFTWARE FOR LANGUAGE 
TRANSLATION 
 
Councilwoman Waski offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Rothwell 
 
WHEREAS, the United States Department of Justice (USDOJ) offers funding for 
various police department initiatives, and 
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead PD is seeking funding for software to provide 
translation language translation capabilities to police body cameras, which is available 
through the USDOJ Safer Outcomes program, and 
 
WHEREAS, the total cost of the equipment is $59,600; and   
 
WHEREAS, the Town of Riverhead will provide a 10% match or $5,960, if funds 
are awarded. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT 
 
RESOLVED, that the Riverhead Town Board hereby authorizes the Riverhead 
Police Department to submit an application through the USDOJ. 
 
RESOLVED that the Town Supervisor is hereby authorized to sign any required 
funding agreements and any associated documents, and be it further 
 
 RESOLVED that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to forward a copy of this 
resolution to the Captain Danielle Willsey, the Community Development Division and 
the Accounting Department, and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of this 
resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified copy of same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
SECONDER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

06.17.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-577 
 
AUTHORIZES THE RIVERHEAD POLICE DEPARTMENT TO APPLY FOR USDOJ 
GRANT TO HIRE POLICE OFFICERS 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
WHEREAS, the United States Department of Justice (USDOJ) offers funding for various 
police department initiatives, and 
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Police Department is seeking funding to hire 3 additional 
officers, which is available through the USDOJ COPS Hiring Program (CHP), and 
 
WHEREAS, CHP awards cover up to 75% of the entry-level salary and fringe benefits 
for each approved position for a three-year funding period with the maximum federal 
share per officer position set at $125,000.00 (over the 3-year period), and 
 
WHEREAS, the total cost of the additional officers will amount to 25% of the established 
starting salary, per officer, per year, for a period of 3 years, and   
 
WHEREAS, the Town of Riverhead will provide a 25% match, if funds are awarded. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED 
 
RESOLVED, that the Riverhead Town Board hereby authorizes the Riverhead Police 
Department to submit an application through the USDOJ. 
 
RESOLVED that the Town Supervisor is hereby authorized to sign any and all required 
funding agreements and any associated documents, and be it further 
 
RESOLVED that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to forward a copy of this 
resolution to the Captain Danielle Willsey, the Community Development Division and 
the Accounting Department, and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of this resolution 
from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified copy of same may be 
obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
SECONDER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski
